## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (single-species population dynamics)
**Analysis**: With features t (time) and P (population size) and target dP_dt (instantaneous growth rate), the task matches continuous-time single-population growth models where dP_dt is governed by density dependence, external forcing, and possible harvesting/mortality terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources, constant per-capita growth)
- Affine source–sink with proportional loss: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (immigration/emigration plus net proportional growth/decay)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric/aggregation effects; super- or sub-exponential growth)
- Logistic-type density dependence (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (self-limitation via carrying capacity ~ 1/c1)
- Generalized (theta) logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible strength/shape of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (logarithmic density dependence; common in tumors/microbial growth)
- Richards (generalized logistic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (extra shape parameter controlling asymmetry)
- Allee effect (weak/strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low density plus carrying capacity)
- Harvesting with constant yield: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant removal; fishery/management scenarios)
- Harvesting with proportional effort: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (linear mortality/harvest rate)
- Saturating harvest (Holling type II on harvest): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (c3 + P) (limited harvesting capacity at high P)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic environment affecting reproduction/survival)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (resource trend changing effective crowding over time)
- Catastrophe/pulse-like mortality (smooth): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P * exp(-c3 * (t - c4)**2) (temporary shock centered at time c4)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth rate structure: writing (dP_dt)/P as a function of P (e.g., c0 - c1*P, log(c1/P)) often indicates density dependence type (linear vs Gompertz).
- Carrying capacity behavior: factors like (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)**k) imply a stable equilibrium near P ≈ 1/c with approach rate set by c0.
- Allee effects: inclusion of a low-density factor such as (c*P - 1) (or equivalently P - threshold) suggests negative growth below a critical population size.
- Harvesting signatures: subtractive terms independent of P (−c) imply constant yield; subtractive terms proportional to P (−c*P) imply proportional mortality/effort; rational harvest terms P/(c+P) imply saturation of removal capacity.
- Environmental seasonality: sin(c*t + phase) multiplying P or the growth-rate term indicates periodic forcing; its amplitude sets cycle strength while c sets period.
- Changing habitat/resources: explicit t-dependence inside the density-regulation factor (e.g., exp(c*t) scaling P) suggests drifting carrying capacity rather than changing intrinsic growth alone.
- Finite-time shocks: localized time kernels like exp(-c*(t-c0)**2) multiplying P indicate transient mortality/reduction events rather than sustained parameter shifts.
- Sub-/super-exponential regimes: dP_dt = c*P**k with k≠1 implies growth accelerates with size (k>1) or slows down even without explicit carrying capacity (k<1).

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

**GT expression:**
`0.1728*(1 - P/48.55)*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(-0.924 + P)))`

Let me simplify:
- First term: `0.1728*P - 0.1728*P²/48.55 = 0.1728*P - 0.003559*P²`
- Second term: `0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*P + 1.408))`

So GT = `c_a*P² + c_b*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*P + 1.408))`

The key structural components are:
1. A **P² term** (quadratic in P)
2. A **P term** (linear in P)
3. A **sigmoid-like term**: `P/(1 + exp(linear in P))` — this involves a logistic/sigmoid function of P

The GT has **no dependence on t**. Any candidate with `t` dependence that cannot be zeroed out is a NO MATCH.

The sigmoid term `P/(1+exp(-aP+b))` is a critical nonlinear component. Let me check what functional forms can match this.

Note: `P/(1+exp(-aP+b))` cannot be expressed as polynomials, simple rational functions P*c/(P+c), power laws P^c, logarithms, or simple exponentials. It requires a sigmoid-type function.

Let me now go through each candidate:

**Candidates with t-dependence that can be zeroed:** If t appears only in terms with free coefficients that can be set to 0, the t-dependence can be eliminated.

**Candidates with no t and no sigmoid-like term:** These cannot match unless they somehow reproduce the sigmoid.

Let me categorize:

**Candidates that are purely polynomial/rational in P (no sigmoid possible):**
- Candidates 15, 16, 17, 18, 19, 20, 27, 31, 33, 34, 35, 36, 50: These are combinations of P², P, P^c, 1/P, P/(P+c), etc. None can produce a sigmoid. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 14:** Rational — **NO MATCH**
